Inevitably the circle of information was widening and it was only a matter of time before the public learned that Bin Laden had been located but Obama hand''t moved [kind of like Clinton with Bin Laden in Somalia and later Afghanistan].  A presidential election was around the corner and rumors that Obama hadn't acted would likely have spelled political doom.<br /><br />Therefore Obama took the chance, Bin Laden died and Obama took the credit.  The author more than hints that his brethren are none too fond of Obama but they are professionals, staged the assault, risked their lives, dealt with problems like a helicopter crash and THEY killed Bin Laden.<br /><br />Ironically, men who likely never voted--or would ever vote for Obama--helped him get reelected.<br /><br />The author isn't surprised that classified information was 'leaked' by the White House.  He is only surprised that vital information on the assault and the assault team was leaked almost immediately.  He never mentions the subsequent targeting of a Seal team helicopter by Taliban/Al Qaeda fighters with the loss of all aboard.  He never mentions that enemy targeting of the Seal team may well have been facilitated by political leaks from the White House.  As the old saying goes, \\"Loose Lips Sink Ships.\\"<br /><br />Administration--Obama--delays in dealing with Bin Laden gives us insights into Obama Presidential performance.  He has real difficulty in dealing quickly and decisively with an emergency.  A point is fact is the massive Administration failure in Benghazi on 9/11/12. So I was very excited when I had the opportunity to read 'Dead Ever After' this past weekend. And right away, when I read Charlaine Harris's words at the beginning, I felt her uncertainty. Meaning, I knew that she had written a book that would probably tick someone off.<br /><br />I loved the book! And I found it to be very realistic. Why? Because Sookie, at heart, is a kind human being. She'd do what she could for you, even if she didn't know you that well. And there is a point in the plot, where in which Sookie's kindness comes back ten fold. She will find herself in a very serious situation and the help she receives to get out of it, will come from the most interesting of people/beings.<br /><br />Sookie's love life ends in a very sensible way as well. After failed romances with vampires, weres and other assorteds, Sookie decides on the hardest working man in that town, that legally makes a living. Is he as exciting as some of the men she has known in the past? Maybe. Maybe not. But 'excitement', mad passion and all of the crap that goes with it, had landed Sookie either in the hospital or with her teeth damned near knocked down her throat. And what's realistic, is that there comes a time where a girl gets tired of nonsense, and just wants a steady guy, who keeps out of trouble.<br /><br />Now I hesitate to bring this up, because I do not approve of disparaging 1 star reviewers, when I am leaving 5 stars, and vice versa. But one of the comments that I kept seeing from the incensed 1 star reviewers, is the phrase 'Sookie doesn't grow. She stays in the same town, in the same job'.<br /><br />I would have to respectfully disagree. Sookie is now a partner in Merlotte's, she was left money that she is going to be getting in monthly sums for the rest of her life. And, sorry to be mean, ignorant or rude, but she's from the South. Do people from there really 'grow'? That confederate flag is proof enough, that there is a certain way that people from that part of the country, like to live and to keep living, for generations. So I did not expect Sookie to leave town, or pick a man, that was very different from herself, in the first place.<br /><br />I actually think that Ms. Harris should wear the bad reviews on here with pride. The only other time I can remember people being this upset, over a piece of fiction, was when 'The Sopranos' ended on HBO. An author should be so fortunate, as to create characters that cause this kind of discussion anywhere. Whether it's good or bad.

B0037TPMOA|5.0|This extraordinary tale of the supernatural opens with arguably the second most famous sentence in the history of western literature:  \\"Jack Torrance thought:  Officious little prick\\".  Obviously this is meant to offend or entrap the reader, and it does, but the comment is not entirely out of context of the character of Jack Torrance once you get to know him .  By the end of part one, we know that he is susceptible to violence, alcoholism and depression.  We also know that the Overlook Hotel - the location of the story itself - has had a particularly violent and gruesome history.  We know that Danny Torrance - son of Jack and Wendy - is gifted (or cursed) with the ability to witness events before they happen.  This is unfortunate for one so young, and yet in this context, this ability may turn out to be a blessing for him to witness events that he does not fully comprehend.<br /><br />As the story progresses, Mr King prefers to hint at significant features of the tale, leading the reader to guess this, or guess that, instead of simply telling the reader what he  wants them to know.  Suspense therefore builds slowly but surely and each page is turned by the reader not just with apprehension of what you know is sure to come, but with a sense of absolute joy in the knowledge that you have placed the next four or five hours of your life in the hands of a master.  And when it comes to The Overlook Hotel, the mind boggles.<br /><br />In summary, then:  Is THE SHINING Stephen King's finest work?  You need to read the book yourself to answer that question. Certainly, one could say CHRISTINE was the greater accomplishment - in it, Mr King made the absurd totally believable (and therefore terrifying).  But with THE SHINING he has turned the everyday, run of the mill ghost story into one of the scariest reading experiences you could ever hope to find.  Reading THE SHINING is like going on an infinite DARE-DOUBLE DARE competition with the devil.  You read one chapter, and then another but then you ask yourself, one more?  one more?  Will i be able to cope with one more?<br /><br />Go on and test yourself, then.  You know you want to.another but then you ask yourself, one more?  one more? This had me in a pool of tears in moments, and that to me is how to sum up the very essence of this book - so many beautiful simple moments that are just so emotionally driven, reading it was honestly exhausting!<br /><br />The characters of Hazel and Augustus are both lovely and while I felt that the banter between the 2 of them was perhaps a little too adult or perhaps a bit staged and melodramatic it still worked as these aren't your run of the mill teenagers with long lives ahead of them. I was impressed with the way the author managed to pull of a female protagonist she was well done, not over the top and really incredibly strong considering all she had faced in her short life so far.<br /><br />For all that this is a pretty depressing topic it is handled really well without glossing over the ugliness of illness.  I read this over 2 nights and found it difficult to put down or stop thinking about.  While this isn't a book I would recommend to everyone - too many of my friends are young mums and I don't think this is really a middle of the night feeding type book, I do think that if you are after something that will make you laugh, cry, smile and most importantly think that this is a fantastic book to read.ith the way the author managed to pull of a female protagonist she was well done, not over the top and really incredibly strong considering all she had faced in her short life so far.<br /><br />For all that this is a pretty depressing topic it is handled really well without glossing over the ugliness of illness. Probably not as I've enjoyed other Kinsella books much more. I'd suggest that they read (or reread) I've Got Your Number or Twenties Girl instead.

B00BSWMITK|3.0|At this point in my life, having been a fan of Joe's since the beginning, I no longer expect him to impress me with his guitar playing skills. I guess I've come to familiarize myself with his style, and his virtuoso playing, that when he pulls off a killer lick or super technical scale run, I just smile and think, \\"Hey, that's Joe for you\\".<br />But what I do expect him to do, and what I expect to hear when I buy his albums on release day without having heard a lick, is MOVE me. Joe, as great as he is a guitar player, is a better songwriter. Or at least he can be. He's got the musical maturity and creativity to do it, time and time again. He achieves this at times with a killer chorus with tons of hook, such as in the songs like \\"If I Could Fly\\" or the underrated \\"Ten Words\\", or sometimes with entire solos that simply ooze with feeling and tastefulness. (Just Look Up, One Robot's Dream, Souls of Distortion, I could go on and on)<br />I realize that songs sometimes grow on you after repeated listenings, but in my experience with Joe's music is that it doesnt take more than a few spins of the entire CD to hear the gems. Gems, as in those moments of music that make the hair on your skin stand-up, or elate your mood with a sudden release of dopamine into your brain. We all have songs that affect us this way. For me, alot of them are from Joe Satriani.<br /><br />So while \\"Unstoppable Momentum\\" is 100% Joe in guitar playing, it falls short in the songwriting arena. It almost sounds like Joe pieced together this album from left-over ideas he had laying around here and there. As a matter of fact, Joe himself has admitted that the song \\"Door into Summer\\" was a melody he had written and then played to the guys in Chickenfoot, only to have it rejected by them, so he stuffed it into his pocket for another day - apparently for this album. Granted, the album has its moments that make me smile, and a few that make me groove, but nothing too memorable or truly impactful. Nothing like his \\"Andalusia\\" or \\"Searching\\", where he just lets it all go from his musical heart. On this latest effort, his prowess may have been captured, but not so much his soul. I still think its better than 99.9% of what passes as music these days, but it's certainly not his best work.ike his \\"Andalusia\\" or \\"Searching\\", where he just lets it all go from his musical heart. On this latest effort, his prowess may have been captured, but not so much his soul. I still think its better than 99.9% of what passes as music these days, but it's certainly not his best work.
